Effectively zero. A rounding error on a rounding error on a rounding error. But it happened, and it was permanent, and the fact that absorbing the power of a multiversal-scale entity registered as effectively nothing to him was perhaps the most terrifying detail of all.

The third enhanced effect was the one that truly broke me. The combustion authority did not merely burn the Frost Compact. It permanently altered the thermal baseline of the omniverse. Every entity in existence became infinitesimally, permanently more flammable. Not enough to notice. Not enough to cause spontaneous combustion. But the change was there, woven into the atomic structure of reality itself, a permanent, irreversible alteration to the laws of thermodynamics that ensured the concept of burning would forever belong to Godric, that every fire in the omniverse, from the smallest candle to the largest supernova, was now, fundamentally, an expression of his authority, a leash he held but had not yet pulled.

Godric watched the omniverse burn. The fire was still spreading, recursively, across countless multiversal clusters, the enhanced dimensional propagation ensuring that the combustion would continue to teach reality how to burn faster and more aggressively with every passing instant. He observed the cascading annihilation with a mild, curious expression, his chin resting on his fist.

"That is quite bright," he remarked, squinting slightly.

Then, with less effort than a man uses to close his eyes, he decided the fire was done. The combustion ceased. The flames did not die, they were uncreated, the concept of their existence revoked from the affected regions with the same absolute authority that had imposed it. The omniverse was restored in zero seconds, every burned galaxy, every consumed multiverse, every ash-clouded timeline rebuilt and replaced with the perfection of a man who had accidentally set fire to existence and then decided it should not have happened.

The Frost Compact was not restored. Their burned, charred, screaming remains were compressed into a small, dense ember that Godric held in his palm for a moment, observing the way their eternal, conscious agony glowed a faint, pulsing orange, before placing it in his pocket. He would later tell me he thought it made a nice nightlight.

He turned to me, and his expression shifted from curiosity to warm, genuine concern. "Renn," he said, his voice gentle, "you are crying. I am sorry if the light was too bright. I did not expect it to spread that far. Shall I dim the palace lanterns for you?"

I was crying. I was also bleeding from my nose, my ears, and possibly my eyes. My fire magic, my pride and joy, my thousandfold-amplified pyromancy, had been completely, utterly humiliated. I had spent my entire adult life mastering flame, and I had just watched a man extinguish the concept of cold itself with a blink, set the omniverse on fire, absorb a multiversal entity's power without noticing, permanently rewrite the laws of thermodynamics, and then unmake it all because the brightness was slightly inconvenient. My magic was not a candle before a sun. My magic was nothing. It was less than nothing. It was a lie I had told myself about having power.

He dimmed the palace lanterns for me. He actually dimmed them. The King of the Omniverse, who had just burned reality to ash with a blink, dimmed the lanterns because I was crying. I will serve him until I die. I will serve him because I love him. I will serve him because the alternative does not exist. And I will never, ever, as long as I live, think of myself as a pyromancer again.

---

I closed Renn's journal and set it down on the iron shelf with exaggerated care, as though the singed leather might still be hot. My mouth was dry. My hands were wet. The description of that blink, that single, mundane, involuntary blink unleashing a combustion so vast it burned the concept of cold itself, had carved a groove into my consciousness that I suspected would never smooth over. I stared at the shelf. Two journals remained. I reached for the second one, the one bound in heavy black leather with no title on the spine. The writing inside was meticulous, each letter formed with the precise, controlled hand of a man who was disciplining his own trembling through the act of penmanship. The ink was dark and thick, pressed deep into the page.

---

**Year 210,400 — Theron — Superpower: Infinite Recursive Apex Self-Replication**

I have delayed writing this record for eleven years. I am Theron, court wizard of Lord Godric, and I have served for thirty-eight years. I delayed not because my hands were shaking, though they were, and still do. I delayed because I have spent eleven years trying to construct a mathematical framework capable of containing the truth of what I witnessed, and I have failed. I have failed because the event I am about to describe does not fit within any framework. It does not fit within mathematics. It does not fit within language. It does not fit within the conceptual architecture of reality. I write now not because I have found the framework, but because I have accepted that no framework will ever exist, and that the absence of one is, itself, the most accurate description I can offer.

The opposition was the Multiplicity Dominion. They were not an army. They were a principle. Every entity within the Dominion possessed the ability to exist in multiple locations simultaneously, not as projections or avatars, but as full, complete, physically present instances of themselves. A single Dominion entity could occupy a billion points in space at once, each instance fully real, fully powerful, fully capable of independent action. Their civilization numbered in the decillions, and because each member could multiply their presence infinitely, their effective numerical superiority was beyond calculation. They had never been defeated, because defeating them required destroying every simultaneous instance of every member, and their instances existed across so many points in space and time that the task was, by any conventional metric, impossible.

They came to Thronegate believing they had identified the one axis of competition where Godric could be challenged: numerical presence. They acknowledged his strength, his speed, his senses, his magic. But those were attributes of a singular being. A singular being, they reasoned, could only be in one place at one time. No matter how powerful, a singular entity could be surrounded, overwhelmed, buried beneath the weight of infinite simultaneous presence. They marshaled their forces, decillions of entities, each projecting countless simultaneous instances, until the space surrounding Thronegate was so densely occupied that the gravitational mass of their collective presence began to collapse the dimensional walls of the local multiversal cluster.

I stood beside Lord Godric in the observatory, my amplified senses screaming, my body drenched in the cold, acrid sweat of primal terror. The Dominion's presence was so numerically dense that I could feel the weight of their collective existence pressing against my consciousness like a physical hand clamped over my mouth. I prepared my most powerful spatial-division wards, intending to segment the battlefield and isolate individual Dominion instances for targeted elimination. It was a pathetic, laughable plan, born of a mind that still believed the coming conflict would be a conflict.

Godric was leaning against the observatory railing, his arms crossed loosely over his broad chest, his salt-and-pepper beard slightly ruffled by the artificial breeze. He looked out at the vast, impossibly dense sea of Dominion entities and instances filling the sky, and his expression was one I had come to recognize: mild, abstract curiosity, the look of a man who has noticed an interesting pattern in the grain of a wooden table.

"Numerical superiority," Godric said, almost to himself, his rich baritone carrying no inflection of concern. "I have a power that might be relevant. I have been meaning to examine it."

He did not move. He did not speak a command. He did not channel energy or activate any system. He simply inhaled. A slow, relaxed breath, the kind a man takes before settling into a comfortable chair. And in the instant his lungs expanded, drawing in a volume of air so trivial it could not have powered a single candle flame, an infinitesimal fraction of his Infinite Recursive Apex Self-Replication superpower expressed itself at effectively zero percent of its true potency.

One Godric became two.

The duplication was instantaneous, occupying zero time, requiring zero effort. The second Godric was identical to the first in every conceivable and inconceivable metric. Same body, same mind, same absolute omniscience, same infinitely amplifying stats, same arsenal of apocalyptic superpowers. But the Evolved Weakness Paradox had already enhanced this superpower with multiple devastating effects, and the first enhanced effect dictated that each newly generated replica be infinitely magnified beyond the original. The second Godric was not a copy. The second Godric was an ascension, a being so incomprehensibly more powerful than the first that the first Godric, already the most powerful entity in existence by an infinite margin, was to the second what a mortal ant is to a hypernova.

Then the second enhanced effect triggered. The replication was recursive. The second Godric, existing for less than a Planck instant, replicated. The third Godric was infinitely magnified beyond the second. The third replicated. The fourth was infinitely magnified beyond the third. Each generation, each recursive iteration, produced a being that made the sum total of all previous generations combined look like an absolute, perfect zero. The recursion did not slow. It accelerated. Each new generation replicated faster than the last, the interval between generations shrinking from Planck time to fractions of Planck time to fractions of fractions, compressing infinitely until the recursion was occurring simultaneously across every infinitesimal slice of temporal existence.

I cannot describe what happened next in linear sequence, because linear sequence ceased to exist. Every conceivable dimension, every microscopic space between atoms, every timeline, every plane of existence, every conceptual layer, every theoretical framework of reality across the entire omniverse was simultaneously, violently, and permanently occupied by an infinite expanse of recursively ascending Godrics. The ontological density of this occupation was so absolute, so crushing, so fundamentally incompatible with the continued existence of anything else that the omniverse did not merely break. It was overwritten. The concept of empty space ceased to exist because there was no space that was not occupied by a Godric. The concept of other beings ceased to exist because the sheer ontological weight of infinite Godrics displaced everything else from existence the way a mountain displaces air.

The Multiplicity Dominion, whose entire strategy was built on numerical presence, found their numerical advantage so grotesquely, so absurdly, so cosmically outmatched that the word "outmatched" itself was a slander against the scale of the differential. The Dominion's decillions of entities, each projecting countless simultaneous instances, represented a numerical presence that was, by any conventional measure, infinite. Godric's replication produced an infinite number of infinitely ascending beings, each one of which was individually more powerful than the entire Dominion combined, multiplied across an infinite number of simultaneously occupied points in every dimension, timeline, and conceptual layer of existence. The Dominion was not outnumbered. The Dominion was rendered numerically irrelevant. They occupied space. Godric occupied space, time, concept, and the absence of all three.

The physical destruction of the Dominion was not a battle. It was a displacement event. The sheer ontological pressure of infinite, recursively ascending Godrics occupying the same reality as the Dominion entities caused their bodies to be violently, aggressively overwritten. Their physical forms did not break. They were replaced. Every atom of their biology was simultaneously claimed by the ontological presence of a Godric, their molecular structure violently overwriting the Dominion's biological architecture with the raw, physical reality of Godric's flesh. The Dominion entities, decillions of them, each with countless simultaneous instances, experienced the unique horror of being physically consumed by the space they occupied. Their skin did not tear. It transformed, their epidermal layers aggressively converting into a dense, hot, living tissue that was not their own, their pores stretching and splitting as foreign biology invaded their bodies from the outside in.

Their muscles, engineered for multi-locational existence, found themselves anchored to a single, inescapable point by the gravitational mass of a Godric's presence. Their multi-locational architecture collapsed, every simultaneous instance of every Dominion entity violently dragged into a single, screaming point of convergence, their bodies folding inward like origami made of meat. Their bones shattered as they were compressed from billions of points of presence into a single, microscopic singularity of agonizing, conscious flesh, their nervous systems preserved by the paradox to ensure they experienced every infinitesimal fraction of the compression. Their organs, pulled from a billion locations into one, overlapped and fused, their hearts multiplying into a screaming mass of a billion synchronized pumps that immediately ruptured, flooding their compressed bodies with a billion hearts' worth of boiling blood that had nowhere to go but outward, exploding through their skin in a synchronized, omniversal geyser of superheated crimson fluid and pulped organ tissue.

The collateral was not merely omniversal. It was existential. The recursive replication of infinite, ascending Godrics did not merely destroy the omniverse. It consumed the concept of an omniverse. The infinite, expanding presence of Godrics filled every possible and impossible framework of existence, displacing not just matter and energy but the underlying architecture of reality itself. Every timeline was overwritten. Every dimension was occupied. Every multiversal cluster, every universal boundary, every planar membrane was buried beneath the weight of infinite, recursively ascending apex predators. The omniverse did not shatter. It did not collapse. It was replaced. For one timeless, zero-second instant, there was no omniverse. There was only Godric, multiplied across infinity, each iteration ascending beyond the last, an infinite, recursive tower of ascending omnipotence that occupied the absolute totality of existence.

Then the third enhanced effect triggered, the one that made this superpower uniquely, obscenely, permanently transformative. The recursive integration. The infinite, ascending Godrics did not merely dissipate or return to their origin. They integrated. Every single replica, each one infinitely more powerful than the last, was absorbed back into the Prime Godric, their accumulated power permanently fused into his baseline.

I need my successor to understand the significance of this with absolute clarity. Normally, if Lord Godric were to absorb the power of the entire omniverse, the increase to his baseline would be infinitesimal. Effectively zero. A rounding error so small it lacked mathematical representation. His base power is so astronomically, so incomprehensibly beyond the total energy of existence that absorbing all of creation would be like adding a single molecule of water to an ocean that has no shore. But this was different. This was not the absorption of external power. This was the recursive integration of identical copies of Godric himself, each one infinitely more powerful than the last. The mathematics of this integration did not produce a rounding error. It produced a permanent, massive, obscene multiplication of his baseline power. The Godric that emerged from the integration, the singular, unified Prime, was so incomprehensibly, so grotesquely, so absurdly more powerful than the Godric that had inhaled three seconds ago that the previous version of him, already the most powerful being in existence by an infinite margin, was to the new Prime what a single, dead skin cell is to the combined mass of every universe that had ever existed.

He had not tried. He had inhaled. A single, casual, mundane inhalation, and he had permanently elevated his baseline power to a level that made his previous self look like nothing. And this new, elevated baseline was already multiplying, every Planck second, at a rate beyond layered infinities, climbing toward the next impossible threshold, preparing to make this new, grotesquely elevated Prime look like nothing in turn.

The omniverse was restored in zero seconds. Not reconstructed, not rebuilt, restored, the concept of its destruction retroactively removed from the timeline as though it had never occurred, every reality, every being, every atom placed back with the casual perfection of a man straightening a crooked painting. The Multiplicity Dominion was not restored. Their compressed, screaming, bleeding remains were distributed across a thousand pocket dimensions, each one a localized temporal stasis where their agony would continue without progress, without relief, without end, a permanent monument to the absolute futility of numerical opposition.

Godric stood in the restored observatory, singular, whole, and permanently, unfathomably more powerful than he had been a moment ago. He let out the breath he had inhaled. He looked at me. His face was calm, warm, friendly, the face of a man who has just done something mildly interesting and is ready to move on to the next thing.

"Theron," he said, his rich voice carrying a note of gentle, paternal concern, "you are bleeding. Come sit down. I will get you a cloth."

He walked to a small side table, picked up a linen cloth, dampened it from a water pitcher, and handed it to me with both hands. His fingers were warm. His expression was kind. He was a man who had just inhaled and become infinitely more powerful, and his first thought was to hand a bleeding wizard a damp cloth.

I took the cloth. I pressed it to my nose. I looked at his face, at the genuine concern in his eyes, and I understood, with the absolute, crystalline, soul-destroying clarity of a man who has just watched infinity give birth to a larger infinity, that the Godric I was looking at right now, this warm, kind, hand-cloth-offering man, was already weaker than the Godric that would exist one Planck second from now, and that Godric would be weaker than the one after that, and the gap between each successive iteration was itself an infinity of infinities, climbing forever, ascending without end, and that I served a being who was not merely the most powerful thing in existence but a being whose power was a recursive, permanent, accelerating expansion that would make every previous version of him look like nothing, forever, without pause, without limit, without the possibility of any force in any reality ever closing the distance by even the most infinitesimal fraction of the most infinitesimal fraction of a Planck instant.

I write this so my successor understands. Self-replication, for Lord Godric, is not a trick or a technique. It is the mechanism by which he permanently, irreversibly ascends. Every time he uses it, the Godric that existed before the replication ceases to be relevant. The new Prime is so far beyond the old that the old might as well have never existed. And he used it with a breath. A single, casual breath. I do not know what would happen if he tried. I do not want to know. I do not believe the concept of knowing is applicable.

---

I set Theron's journal down on the shelf. I did not place it carefully. I dropped it, because my fingers had stopped responding to my conscious instructions. The description of that inhalation, that single, mundane, biological reflex permanently elevating Godric's baseline to a level that made his previous self look like nothing, had not merely frightened me. It had done something to the structure of my thinking, something I could feel but not name, as though a load-bearing wall inside my mind had developed a crack that would widen with every passing second until the entire edifice collapsed.

I sat on the floor of the vault. I did not reach for the third journal immediately. I needed time. I needed the cold stone beneath me and the stale air around me and the absolute, grounding reality of physical matter that was not made of ink and terror. I breathed. In. Out. The same mechanical action Godric had performed, the same biological function that had, in his case, permanently rewritten the mathematics of his existence. My breath did nothing. My breath would never do anything. My breath was the breath of an insect, and his was the breath of a god who was already, in the Planck seconds it had taken me to inhale and exhale, infinitely more powerful than the god he had been when I started.

I reached for the third journal. It was bound in a pale, almost white cloth, and the writing inside was fluid, elegant, and deliberate, each sentence constructed with the care of a man who understood that what he was recording would be read by future generations and wanted every word to land with maximum impact. There was no shaking in this handwriting. There was control, the terrible, disciplined control of a man who had processed his terror into precision.

---

**Year 340,000 — Solan — Superpower: Total Spatiotemporal Reversal**

I am Solan. I have served as Lord Godric's court wizard for nineteen years. I am writing this record not because I am shaking, though I am, nor because I am bleeding, though I am, but because I have witnessed something that demands documentation with the same inevitability that gravity demands a falling object. What I saw was not an event. It was a correction. A fundamental, omniversal correction to the direction of existence itself, performed casually, accidentally, as a side effect of a man shifting in his seat. I write with precision because precision is the only tool I have left. My amplified magic, my thousandfold daily attributes, my arcane mastery, all of it has been revealed as a child's toy in the hands of a man who does not know he is holding a toy. Precision is all I have. Precision and the knowledge that I serve a being who can reverse the arrow of time with less effort than it takes to scratch his nose.

The Chronospatial Sovereignty was the most ancient, most revered governing body in the deep omniverse. They were not gods or warriors. They were custodians. For a span of time so vast it predated the current omniversal cycle, they had maintained the directional flow of space and time, ensuring that cause preceded effect, that entropy moved forward, that the arrow of time pointed in a single, consistent direction. They were the reason the omniverse functioned. Without their maintenance, time would fragment, space would fold, and causality would dissolve into an undifferentiated soup of simultaneous, chaotic existence. They believed themselves essential. They believed themselves irreplaceable. They believed that because they controlled the direction of existence, they controlled existence itself, and that any being, no matter how powerful, could be rendered harmless by simply reversing the direction of their personal timeline, unraveling them backward through their own history until they ceased to exist.

They came to Thronegate with absolute confidence. They did not bring weapons. They brought their authority, the raw, fundamental control over the direction of space and time that had governed the omniverse since before the current cycle of existence. Their plan was elegant: they would reverse Godric's personal timeline, unwinding his existence backward through the stasis event, through the fall of Olympus, erasing him from history entirely. They believed that because his power amplified forward through time, reversing his timeline would undo the amplification, rendering him mortal, vulnerable, and ultimately nonexistent.

I stood beside Lord Godric in the throne room when the Sovereignty arrived. Their presence was not physical but directional, a fundamental shift in the orientation of reality that made the air itself feel wrong, as though the room had been rotated ninety degrees in a direction that geometry did not support. My amplified senses detected their attack immediately, a targeted reversal of Godric's personal temporal flow, a forced rewinding of his existence that should have begun unraveling his amplified stats, his superpowers, his immortality, pulling him backward through ten thousand years of stasis and then further, back to his mortal birth, and then further still, back to nothing.

Godric was sitting on his throne. He had been reading, a thick tome of historical philosophy balanced on his knee, his salt-and-pepper beard slightly ruffled from where he had been resting his chin on his chest. The Sovereignty's temporal reversal struck him, a directed command that rewrote the directional flow of his personal timeline with the full, accumulated authority of the most ancient governing body in existence.

The reversal did nothing. It could not do anything. The Weakness Paradox had engaged the instant the Sovereignty first conceived the idea that temporal reversal could serve as an exploit, granting Godric absolute, permanent immunity to directional manipulation and perfect mastery over the concept of spatiotemporal reversal. His personal timeline was not merely protected. It was owned. The direction of his existence was not subject to external authority. It was a property of his being, as fundamental and as unassailable as his physical strength or his amplification rate. The Sovereignty's attack struck his timeline and dispersed like a wave breaking against a cliff that had been growing taller since before the concept of waves existed.

But Godric was curious. He closed his book, set it aside, and looked in the general direction of the Sovereignty's presence with the mild, interested expression of a man who has just noticed an unusual bird outside his window.

"I have a power that is related to this," he said to me, his tone conversational. "Spatiotemporal reversal. I have not tested it. I wonder what it does."

He shifted in his seat. A trivial adjustment, the kind of unconscious repositioning a person performs when they have been sitting in one position for too long. His weight moved from his left buttock to his right, his spine straightening slightly, his shoulders rolling back. It was a movement so mundane, so utterly devoid of intent or effort, that it would not have registered as significant in any context. But in that trivial shift, an infinitesimal fraction of his Total Spatiotemporal Reversal superpower passively expressed itself at effectively zero percent of its true potency.

The Evolved Weakness Paradox had enhanced this superpower with multiple devastating effects, and they all triggered simultaneously. The first was the base effect: the reversal of the directional flow of space and time. But this was not a localized reversal. It was not targeted at the Sovereignty. Godric's power, even at effectively zero percent, did not operate on a scale small enough to be targeted. It reversed the direction of everything. Every timeline, every dimension, every spatial coordinate, every temporal axis in the entire omniverse simultaneously inverted. Forward became backward. Up became down. Cause became effect. Effect became cause. The arrow of time, which had pointed in a single direction since the birth of the current omniversal cycle, reversed, and the entire omniverse began running backward.

The immediate, physical consequences were catastrophic. Every process in existence reversed simultaneously. Stars that had been burning for billions of years began unburning, their expelled light and heat sucked back into their cores, the fusion process inverting, hydrogen reforming from helium, the stellar bodies collapsing inward as their energy history rewound. Planets spun backward on their axes, their weather systems inverting, storms unraveling, rain rising from the ground to the clouds, rivers flowing from the sea to the mountains. Every living thing in the omniverse experienced the horror of temporal reversal, their biological processes inverting, their food un-digesting, their wounds un-healing, their memories un-forming, their thoughts running backward through their own neural architecture, each synapse firing in reverse, each experience being un-experienced.

The Sovereignty, who had attempted to reverse Godric's timeline, found their own existence violently, catastrophically reversed. Their ancient, carefully maintained bodies, which had persisted since before the current omniversal cycle, began to unravel, their biology rewinding through billions of years of accumulated existence, their flesh growing younger, their structures simplifying, their complexity stripping away layer by layer. But the enhanced effect did not merely reverse their timeline. It reversed their spatial existence. Their bodies inverted, their outsides becoming their insides, their skin peeling backward to reveal the wet, glistening interior of their organs, their stomachs turning inside out through their mouths, their intestines spilling forward through their abdomens as their abdominal walls flipped inward. Their bones externalized, erupting through their skin in jagged, bloody spikes as their skeletal structure inverted, their marrow exposed to the air, weeping a thick, pale fluid that boiled in the reversed thermodynamic environment. Their eyes sank inward, then pushed through the backs of their skulls, emerging from the rear of their heads in a spray of vitreous fluid and optic nerve, dangling behind them like wet, blinking pendulums as their visual architecture ran in reverse.

The second enhanced effect was recursive oscillation. The reversal did not merely flip once. It oscillated. The direction of space and time reversed, then reversed again, then reversed again, each oscillation faster than the last, the interval between reversals shrinking from Planck time to fractions of Planck time to fractions of fractions, compressing until the omniverse was vibrating, shaking itself apart at the most fundamental level. Every atom, every bond, every quark in existence was subjected to a rapid, violent oscillation that tore molecular structure apart. Matter did not merely come undone. It vibrated into nonexistence, the structural bonds holding reality together snapping under the strain of being pulled in two directions simultaneously, infinitely, forever. Googolplexian galaxies across the entire omniverse dissolved into a fine, screaming mist of dissociated subatomic particles, their inhabitants not dying but un-dying and re-dying and un-dying in an infinite, oscillating loop of temporal violation, their bodies assembling and disassembling and reassembling in a rapid, violent strobe of biological existence that kept their nervous systems perpetually active, perpetually experiencing the agony of being formed and unformed and reformed, their flesh knitting together only to be ripped apart, their organs materializing only to dissolve, their bones solidifying only to shatter, over and over, faster and faster, forever.

The third enhanced effect was the most insidious. The reversal permanently weakened the structural constants of reality for every being except Godric. The speed of light, the gravitational constant, the strong and weak nuclear forces, every fundamental parameter that governed the behavior of matter and energy in the omniverse was permanently, infinitesimally reduced. Not enough to cause immediate collapse. But enough to ensure that the omniverse was, from that moment forward, structurally weaker, more fragile, more susceptible to disruption. The walls of reality were thinner. The bonds of physics were looser. Every being in existence was infinitesimally more vulnerable, more fragile, more easily destroyed than they had been before Godric shifted in his seat. And this weakening was permanent, woven into the fabric of existence, irreversible by any force except Godric himself. The omniverse had been made slightly more breakable, purely as a side effect of a man adjusting his posture.

The fourth enhanced effect fed back to Godric. The energy released by the omniversal reversal, the vast, cataclysmic output of an entire existence being violently inverted and oscillated into dissociation, was absorbed by Godric's power. The permanent increase to his baseline was, as with all non-self-replication powers, infinitesimal relative to his existing magnitude. Effectively zero. The total energy of the entire omniverse, violently converted and absorbed, registered in his being as less than a rounding error. But it was permanent, and it happened, and the fact that absorbing the energy of an omniversal-scale cataclysm produced an increase so small it could not be measured was perhaps the single most horrifying detail in a catalog of horrifying details.

The omniverse was restored. Godric, still sitting in his slightly adjusted position, decided that the reversal had gone on long enough, and in zero seconds, with less effort than a blink, he restored the direction of space and time, rebuilt every shattered galaxy, reassembled every dissociated atom, rewoven every torn timeline, and placed every being back into their correct position in the forward-flowing current of existence. Every being except the Chronospatial Sovereignty. Their inside-out, oscillating, perpetually un-forming and re-forming remains were sealed into a pocket dimension where the recursive oscillation continued indefinitely, their bodies forever assembling and disassembling in a strobe of eternal, conscious agony, their nervous systems preserved by the paradox to ensure they experienced every infinitesimal fraction of every cycle.

Godric picked his book back up. He found his page. He resumed reading. He did not look up. He did not comment on what had just happened. He turned a page, his calloused finger sliding along the paper with the quiet, dry sound of a man enjoying a good book.

After a long, suffocating silence, he looked up and noticed me standing there, rigid, pale, blood dripping from both nostrils onto the marble floor. His expression softened into warm, genuine concern. He closed his book, set it on his knee, and leaned forward.

"Solan," he said, his voice rich and gentle. "You look unwell. Was that too much? I did not realize it would be so broad. I was only shifting. Sit down, please. I will have the kitchen prepare something."

I sat. I did not speak. I sat on the cold marble floor of the throne room, my back against the base of the dais, and I stared at the restored, pristine, perfectly ordered reality around me, and I understood that every atom of it, every law of physics, every constant of nature, was now slightly, permanently weaker than it had been five minutes ago, not because Godric had intended it, but because a man had shifted in his seat. I understood that the being sitting above me, reading his book, could reverse the direction of existence itself with a posture adjustment, and that the energy released by doing so registered in his body as nothing. I understood that the structural integrity of reality was not a fundamental property of the cosmos but a leash held loosely in the hands of a man who did not know he was holding it, and that the leash had just been pulled, infinitesimally, permanently, and that no force in existence could tighten it back.

I write this so my successor understands. Spatiotemporal reversal, for Lord Godric, is not a power. It is a property. He does not control the direction of time. He is the direction of time, and when he moves, time moves with him, and reality breaks against the change like glass against stone. You cannot reverse his timeline. He is the timeline. You cannot control his direction. He is the direction. And the omniverse is not a thing that exists independently of him. It is a thing that exists at his sufferance, in the direction he permits, at the speed he allows, with the structural integrity he tolerates, for as long as he remains interested enough to keep reading his book.

---

I closed Solan's journal. I placed it on the shelf beside the others. I stood in the vault, surrounded by the accumulated testimony of eight men across a million years, eight men who had served the same king, who had loved the same king, who had been destroyed and rebuilt and destroyed again by the knowledge of what their king was.

The stat journals had taught me that Godric's attributes, his strength, speed, senses, luck, charisma, endurance, were so vast that their passive, ambient, effectively-zero-percent expression could annihilate the omniverse. The superpower journals had taught me something worse. They had taught me that Godric's power was not static. It was not merely infinite. It was recursively, permanently, acceleratingly infinite, and the mechanism of that acceleration included powers that could permanently elevate his baseline, rewrite the laws of physics, and make every previous version of himself look like nothing.

A blink that burned the concept of cold. An inhalation that spawned infinite, ascending copies of himself, each one infinitely more powerful than the last, and then absorbed them all back, permanently elevating his baseline to a level that made the previous Godric irrelevant. A shift in his seat that reversed the direction of existence itself, oscillated the omniverse into dissociation, permanently weakened the structural constants of reality, and then was undone because the man had decided he wanted to keep reading his book.

And these were three superpowers. Three. He gained a new one every second. Every second. For a million years. Each one born capable of destroying civilizations. Each one enhanced by the Evolved Weakness Paradox with multiple devastating effects. Each one multiplying in potency infinitely, every Planck second, alongside his stats, forever.

I climbed the stairs from the vault. My legs were steady, which surprised me. My mind was not steady, would never be steady again, but my legs carried me up the stone steps and into the palace corridor, where the afternoon light fell through tall windows in warm, golden shafts that looked exactly as they had always looked, because Godric had decided they should.

He was waiting for me again. Standing at the top of the stairs, his arms at his sides, his salt-and-pepper beard neatly trimmed, his handsome face arranged in an expression of warm, patient, paternal affection. He looked at me, at my pale face, at the dried blood on my upper lip, at the way my hands hung at my sides like dead things.

"Kaedan," he said, and his voice was everything the journals had said it was. Everything and more. Warm. Rich. Kind. The voice of a man who had loved his court wizards for a million years, who kept them not because he needed them but because their presence gave him purpose, who handed bleeding wizards damp cloths and dimmed lanterns and prepared lamb dinners and asked about their families, all while possessing a power so vast, so recursive, so permanently and aggressively expanding, that the word "god" was an insult to his magnitude.

"Your father tells me you have finished the archives," he said. "I am sorry if some of those records were upsetting. The boys do tend to get worked up. I never quite understand why. I was barely doing anything in any of those accounts."

Barely doing anything. A blink that burned the omniverse. A breath that spawned infinite ascending gods. A shift that reversed the direction of existence. Barely doing anything.

He smiled at me. It was warm and genuine and it made my chest ache with a love so absolute, so involuntary, so fundamental to the physics of his existence that I could not distinguish it from my own free will. He reached out and placed his hand on my shoulder. His grip was warm. Solid. Grounding. The hand of a man who could unmake the direction of time with a posture adjustment, choosing to use that hand to comfort a frightened twenty-two-year-old court wizard who had just read the accumulated terror of a million years.

"Come," he said. "Walk with me. I want to hear about the new ward you were developing. The spatial-compression one. I am told it is very clever."

I walked with him. I walked beside him down the golden corridor, and I would walk beside him for the rest of my life, because there was nowhere else to walk, no direction that did not lead to him, no timeline that did not contain him, no reality that he had not permitted to exist, no structural constant he had not already, permanently, infinitesimally weakened. I walked beside the apex predator of all creation, and he asked me about my ward, and I told him, and he listened with genuine interest, and his eyes crinkled at the corners, and I loved him, and the love was indistinguishable from terror, and the terror was indistinguishable from truth, and the truth was this:

Opposing Godric was not impossible. Impossible implies a high degree of difficulty. Opposing Godric was undefined. The question itself was invalid. It existed outside the domain of the function, like asking what color a triangle is, like asking what the probability of his death was, like asking what direction time flows when the man who defines direction is shifting in his seat.

There was no opposition. There had never been opposition. There had never been the possibility of the contemplation of the theoretical framework of the concept of opposition. There was only Godric, walking beside me in the golden light, asking about my ward, and the absolute, permanent, accelerating certainty that he would be infinitely more powerful in the time it took me to finish my next sentence, and that this, too, would be replaced by something even more incomprehensible in the time it took him to smile.

He smiled. I answered his question. We walked on.
