Every atom, every particle, every quantum fluctuation, every dimensional membrane, every temporal axis, every conceptual foundation, every being, every structure, every thing that existed or could exist or had ever existed or would ever exist in any possible or impossible configuration of reality, was compressed by the pressure wave into the same, sub-Planck-scale, infinitesimally minute point of infinite mass.

The entire omniverse was compressed. Not destroyed. Not annihilated. Compressed. Every reality, every timeline, every dimension, every multiversal cluster, every civilization, every god, every machine, every entity, every living thing, every dead thing, every thing that had ever existed or could ever exist or had ever been imagined or conceived or theorized or dreamt, was squeezed, crushed, condensed, de-atomized, and compressed into a single point so small, so infinitesimally, so impossibly minute that it existed below the smallest measurable scale in any framework of physics, a point of infinite mass and zero volume that contained, within its unimaginable density, the absolute totality of everything that had ever been or could ever be.

The process took less than a fraction of a Planck second. To a mortal observer, if one had existed, which none did, because all mortal observers had been compressed into the point, the event would have been instantaneous. Undetectable. A single, frameless instant in which everything that existed was reduced to a point smaller than a quark. But to the beings compressed within the point, their consciousness preserved by the cruel, precise, absolute force of Godric's effectively-zero-percent strength, the process was experienced as an eternity of maximum-capacity agony, the sensation of being de-atomized, of feeling every atom of their being crushed past the nuclear shell, past the quark structure, into a state of compression so extreme that the concept of compression itself had been surpassed and replaced by something that physics could not name.

Godric stood in the void. The void was absolute. There was nothing around him. No stars, no galaxies, no universes, no dimensions, no timelines, no reality, no void. There was only Godric, standing in the nothing, his dark clothes unruffled, his beard immaculate, his expression carrying the mild, sheepish, slightly apologetic quality of a man who had accidentally knocked something over.

The point floated before him. A single, infinitesimally small, sub-Planck-scale point of infinite mass, containing the compressed totality of everything that had ever existed or could ever exist, hung in the air at chest height, its gravitational pull so vast that it should have consumed Godric himself, should have consumed everything, should have torn the fabric of non-existence apart with the sheer, impossible density of its being. But it did not, because the point was Godric's, created by his strength, held by his will, and nothing that Godric created could harm Godric.

He reached out and picked it up. His thick, calloused fingers, the same fingers that had been built hauling logs in a kingdom called Olympus, closed around the point with the casual, effortless ease of a man picking up a pebble from a beach. The point, which contained the compressed infinite mass of the entire possible existence, which contained every reality, every timeline, every dimension, every being, every thing, weighed nothing. Not a small something. Nothing. The infinite mass of all existence, compressed into a point smaller than a quark, registered in Godric's hand as less than nothing, as a weight so infinitesimally, so cosmically, so structurally insignificant relative to his strength that the act of holding it required less effort than the act of breathing, and breathing required no effort, because breathing was a habit, not a necessity.

He examined the point, holding it between his thumb and forefinger, squinting at it with the expression of a man examining a speck of dust on his sleeve. Then, with a casual, almost bored flick of his fingers, he enlarged it. Not expanded. Enlarged. He manipulated the spatial coordinates of the point's container, stretching the barrier that held it until the point was the size of a marble, a small, smooth, perfectly round sphere that sat in his palm and pulsed with a faint, inner light, the compressed, screaming, eternally agonizing consciousness of everything that had ever existed flickering within it like a trapped star.

He held up the marble. He looked at it, turning it this way and that, examining the way the light caught its surface. It was, I realized, a trophy. A keepsake. A memento of the last opposition, the final game, the last time anyone would ever dare to approach the apex predator of all creation with anything other than absolute, total, unconditional surrender. The marble contained everything. Every reality, every timeline, every being, every thing that had ever existed or could ever exist, compressed into a sphere the size of a child's toy, held in the hand of a man who was disappointed that his show had been boring.

Then, with less thought than a man uses to blink, Godric restored everything. In zero seconds, with zero effort, he rebuilt the omniverse. Every reality, every timeline, every dimension, every multiversal cluster, every civilization, every god, every machine, every entity, every being that had been compressed into the marble was recreated, rebuilt, placed back exactly where they had been, their memories intact, their minds permanently scarred by the experience of having been de-atomized and compressed into a sub-Planck-scale point of infinite mass and maximum agony. The restoration was perfect. Identical. Every atom in the same position, every quantum state in the same configuration, every timeline following the same path, every being possessing the same memories, the same identities, the same histories.

Everything was restored. Everything except the coalition. The fictional champions, the trillion beings from a thousand fictional realities who had banded together to oppose Godric, were not restored. Their compressed, screaming, eternally agonizing consciousness remained in the marble, preserved forever, a permanent, infinitesimal, screaming point of maximum suffering that Godric kept because he found it amusing.

The marble remained in his pocket. It remained there as he walked back to the palace, as he resumed his routine, as he sat in his study and opened a book and began to read. It remained there, a small, smooth, perfectly round sphere the size of a child's toy, containing the compressed infinite mass of the entire possible existence, sitting in the pocket of a man who was reading a history of pre-Stasis Olympian agriculture and who had, an hour ago, been disappointed that a coalition of fictional characters had failed to entertain him.

---

I closed Osvald's journal. My hands were not shaking. They had passed beyond shaking, the same way Osvald's hands had passed beyond shaking, the same way every court wizard's hands eventually passed beyond shaking, arriving at a place where the fear was so total, so complete, so structurally integrated into every fiber of my being, that my body had stopped trying to express it.

The marble. The marble was still in Godric's pocket. I had seen it, many times, without understanding what it was. A small, smooth sphere, the size of a child's toy, that Godric sometimes took out and examined with the mild, nostalgic affection of a man looking at a souvenir. I had assumed it was a decorative item. A trinket. A keepsake of no particular significance.

It contained the compressed infinite mass of the entire possible existence. Every reality, every timeline, every dimension, every being, every thing that had ever existed or could ever exist, compressed into a sphere the size of a marble, screaming eternally in a state of maximum agony, held in the pocket of a man who had created it accidentally, with effectively zero percent of his strength, because he was disappointed that a show was boring.

And he had restored everything. He had rebuilt the omniverse. Every reality, every timeline, every being, placed back exactly where they had been, identical, perfect, indistinguishable from the originals.

But the originals were still in the marble.

I sat with this knowledge. I sat with it in the dark, in my chambers, in the palace that existed on a world that orbited a star that existed in a universe that existed in a multiverse that existed in an omniverse that was, I now understood, a copy. A perfect, identical, indistinguishable copy, rebuilt from nothing by a man who had compressed the original into a marble and put it in his pocket and gone back to reading his book. The universe I inhabited, the air I breathed, the stone beneath my feet, the blood in my veins, the memories in my mind, the love I felt for my family, the fear I felt for my king, all of it was a reproduction. A flawless, atom-perfect reproduction, created in zero seconds by a being whose effectively-zero-percent strength had been sufficient to compress the original into a point smaller than a quark and then rebuild it from nothing.

Was it real? The question was not philosophical. It was structural. The restored omniverse was identical to the original. Every atom in the same position. Every quantum state in the same configuration. Every timeline following the same path. By every measurable, theoretical, and conceptual metric, the restored omniverse was the original omniverse. There was no difference. No flaw. No imperfection. The copy was the original, and the original was the copy, and the distinction between them was meaningless, because the being who had made the copy had made it with a perfection so absolute that the copy and the original were, in every way that mattered, the same thing.

But the original was still in the marble. Still screaming. Still compressed. Still suffering. The real omniverse, the first omniverse, the one that had existed before Godric's disappointment had triggered an immune response that compressed everything into a point, was still in his pocket, a trophy, a toy, a keepsake, eternally agonizing, eternally conscious, eternally aware that it had been compressed into a marble by a man who had not been trying.

I lived in a copy. I lived in a reproduction. I lived in a universe that had been rebuilt from nothing by a being who had compressed the original into a marble and kept it as a souvenir. And the copy was perfect, and the perfection was the horror, because the perfection meant that I could not tell the difference, that no one could tell the difference, that the being I served, the being I loved, the being who dimmed my lanterns and asked about my family, had the power to compress the entire omniverse into a marble, restore it perfectly, and keep the original in his pocket, and no one, anywhere, in any timeline, in any reality, in any possible or impossible configuration of existence, would ever know.

This was the fear. This was the fear that had broken my father, that had broken Osvald, that had broken every court wizard who had read this journal and understood its implications. Not the fear of Godric's power. Not the fear of his strength, his speed, his magic, his auras, his immune system. The fear of his casualness. The fear of a being so powerful that compressing the entire omniverse into a marble was an accident, a side effect of a sigh, a trivial, involuntary consequence of being disappointed by a boring show. The fear of a being who could reproduce the omniverse from nothing, perfectly, in zero seconds, and keep the original in his pocket as a toy. The fear of a being for whom the entire possible existence was a thing that could be compressed, restored, compressed again, restored again, manipulated, rewritten, discarded, recreated, without effort, without thought, without consequence, without meaning, because the existence was his, and he could do with it what he wanted, and what he wanted was to be entertained, and the entertainment had been boring, and the boredom had compressed everything into a marble, and the marble was still in his pocket, and I was living in the copy, and the copy was perfect, and the perfection was the horror, and the horror was forever.

And the fear, the final, deepest, most structurally devastating fear, was the knowledge that this had been the last opposition. Not because Osvald knew. He had not known, when he wrote the journal, that the coalition he documented would be the final coalition. He had written it as a routine record, a warning for his successor, a processing of trauma. But the omniverse had learned. The omniverse, the restored copy, the perfect reproduction, had learned, through the experience of being compressed into a marble and restored, that opposition was not merely futile. Opposition was an inconvenience. And Godric's immune system responded to inconveniences. And the response was the compression of everything into a marble. And the marble was still in his pocket. And no one, anywhere, in any timeline, in any reality, wanted to be in the marble.

No one opposed Godric again. Not because he altered free will. Not because he suppressed the impulse. Not because he removed the cognitive architecture that allowed the thought of opposition to form. But because the omniverse, the restored, perfect, identical copy of the omniverse, had experienced, firsthand, the consequence of opposition, and the consequence was the marble, and the marble was forever, and forever was a long time to be compressed into a sphere smaller than a quark, screaming, while the man who put you there read a book about agriculture and occasionally took you out of his pocket to admire you.

The opposition ended. Not with a battle. Not with a war. Not with a climactic, narratively-satisfying final confrontation between good and evil, between freedom and tyranny, between the heroes and the final boss. It ended with a sigh. A disappointed sigh. A man's genuine, sincere, unfeigned expression of letdown at a boring show, and the sigh had compressed everything into a marble, and the marble was in his pocket, and the pocket was Godric, and Godric was forever.

I set the journal on the shelf. I did not return it to the vault. I did not hide it. I placed it on the shelf, in the open, where my successor would find it, because my successor needed to find it, because my successor needed to understand, as I now understood, as Osvald had understood, as every court wizard who had read this journal had understood, that the being they served was not merely the most powerful entity in existence. He was the being for whom existence was a marble. A toy. A keepsake in a pocket. And the pocket was warm, and the man was kind, and the lanterns were dim, and the copy was perfect, and the perfection was the horror, and the horror was the truth, and the truth was Godric, and Godric was forever.

----------------------------------

## ./prompts/prompt24_godric_vs_god.md
*outputs/glm_20260706_151111.md*

The second journal was thinner than the first. Its binding was plain, unmarked, a simple dark cover with no title, no author, no indication of the contents within. It had been placed behind Osvald's first journal on the same shelf, deliberately obscured, as though my predecessor had tried to hide it from view, or from memory, or from the future itself. The pages inside were not written in ink. They were written in something that had the color and consistency of ink but that my amplified senses, straining against the substance with every ounce of my thousandfold-daily-multiplied perception, could not identify. It was not blood. It was not dye. It was not any fluid produced by any biological process I could name. It was, I suspected, the only substance Osvald's body had been capable of producing after what he had witnessed, a secretion born not of physiology but of necessity, his body generating a writing medium from sheer, desperate need to record, because the act of recording was the only thing keeping his consciousness from dissolving into the same screaming, compressed nothing that the marble in Godric's pocket contained.

I opened the journal. The handwriting was not the steady, controlled script of the first record. It was jagged, fractured, the letters formed by a hand that was operating on the residual momentum of a man who had already broken and was simply going through the mechanical motions of documentation because the alternative was to stop, and stopping meant thinking, and thinking meant remembering, and remembering meant reliving, and reliving meant experiencing, again, the thing that Osvald had spent every moment since the incident trying to forget.

My name is Clive. I am fifty years old. I am the Royal Court Wizard of Thronegate. I have read the journals of my predecessors. I have read Osvald's first journal, the record of the fictional coalition, the last opposition that any being in the omniverse dared to form against Godric. I believed, when I finished that journal, that I had reached the limit of what could be feared. I believed that the marble, the compressed totality of existence sitting in Godric's pocket, was the final horror, the ultimate demonstration of the gap between Godric and everything else.

I was wrong. The marble was not the final horror. The marble was the penultimate horror. The final horror was the thing that came after the marble, the thing that Osvald documented in this second, hidden journal, the thing that had been so devastating to his psyche that he had buried the record behind his first journal and never spoken of it, never referenced it, never acknowledged its existence to his successor, my father, who had found it only by accident, who had read it only once, and who had placed it in my hands with a grip that left crescent moons in my palms and an expression of raw, primal, animal fear on his face.

The thing that came after the marble was God.

---

**Journal of Osvald, Age 44, Court Wizard of Thronegate — The True Final Opposition**

I am writing this in the dark. I have extinguished every light in my chambers. I have sealed the door. I have constructed seventeen layers of arcane warding around my study, not for protection, because nothing can protect me from the knowledge I now carry, but for isolation, because I need the darkness and the silence and the isolation to process what I have witnessed, and I am using the word process in the mechanical sense, the way a machine processes raw material, because my mind is no longer functioning as a mind. It is functioning as a machine, grinding through the implications of what I saw, reducing them to component parts, assembling them into a record, because the record is the only thing that is real, and reality is the only thing I have left, and reality, I now understand, may not even be real.

God came to Thronegate. I must state this plainly, without embellishment, without qualification, because the plainness of the statement is its own horror. God. The Creator. The supreme being. The entity that, across every civilization, every mythology, every theology, every cosmological framework that had ever existed in any reality in the omniverse, was understood to be the origin. The first cause. The unmoved mover. The being who had created existence itself, who had fashioned the omniverse from nothing, who had breathed life into the first atom and set the first quantum fluctuation in motion and established the fundamental constants that governed the behavior of matter and energy across every dimension and every timeline. God. The maker of everything. The architect of reality. The source.

God came to Thronegate, and God came to oppose Godric.

I need to contextualize this, because the context is the horror. God was not a cosmic entity. God was not a pantheon head, not a conceptual abstraction, not a collective consciousness, not a hyper-dimensional being. God was God. The singular, supreme, absolute Creator of everything that existed, had ever existed, or would ever exist. By every theological, philosophical, and ontological framework ever devised by any mind in any reality, God was the ceiling. God was the being beyond which nothing could exist, because God had created everything, and the creator was, by definition, greater than the creation. God's power was the power of genesis, of ex nihilo creation, of the ability to call forth reality from nothingness. God's knowledge was the knowledge of the architect, encompassing every detail of the structure He had built. God's presence was the presence of the source, the fundamental, foundational existence from which all other existence flowed.

God was, by any standard that the omniverse could apply, the most powerful being in existence. And God came to Thronegate to oppose Godric.

I stood beside Lord Godric on the observation platform when God arrived. The arrival was not dramatic. There was no thunder, no blinding light, no tearing of the dimensional fabric. God simply was. One moment, the space before the platform was empty. The next, God occupied it. He appeared as a figure of such absolute, such foundational, such ontologically primary presence that my amplified senses could not process Him as a visual phenomenon. I could not see God the way I saw other beings. I perceived Him the way I perceived gravity, or time, or the strong nuclear force, as a fundamental, structural fact of reality, a constant that had always existed and that my senses were only now acknowledging because it had chosen to manifest in a form that was, for the first time, distinct from the reality it had created.

God's form was not a body. It was a focal point, a location in space where the Creator had chosen to concentrate His presence, and the concentration was so vast, so total, so incomprehensibly dense with creative authority that the surrounding reality responded to His proximity the way a painting responds to the presence of its painter. The stars in the surrounding galaxies brightened. The dimensional walls of the local multiversal cluster became transparent, then luminous, then radiant, the fabric of existence itself recognizing its maker and straining toward Him with the desperate, reverent yearning of a creation acknowledging its source. The laws of physics, the constants that governed the behavior of matter and energy, flexed and hummed in God's presence, the speed of light increasing fractionally, the gravitational constant deepening, the strong and weak nuclear forces tightening, as though the fundamental parameters of reality were trying to impress their father, to show Him that they were functioning well, that they were doing what He had designed them to do.

I fell to my knees. Not from fear, though fear was present. From reverence. The reverence was involuntary, biological, a response encoded in the deepest, most foundational layer of my being, the layer that understood, at a level beneath thought, beneath instinct, beneath consciousness, that the being before me was the source of everything I was. My atoms recognized their architect. My mana recognized its origin. My soul, if I had one, recognized its maker. Every component of my existence, from the quantum structure of my subatomic particles to the amplified architecture of my thousandfold-multiplied magical core, responded to God's presence with the total, absolute, involuntary submission of a creation acknowledging its creator.

God spoke. His voice was not a sound. It was a reality. When God spoke, the words He uttered did not travel through the air. They rewrote the air. The medium of transmission was not vibration but creation, each syllable calling into existence a new fundamental truth that replaced the old one, the air around Him becoming a substance that carried meaning rather than sound, a living, conscious medium that understood what it was transmitting and trembled with the weight of it.

"I am the Creator," God said, and the statement was not a claim. It was a fact, as fundamental as the existence of space, as inescapable as the passage of time. "I made all that is. I made the omniverse, the multiverses, the universes, the dimensions, the timelines, the conceptual frameworks, the laws of physics, the principles of magic, the architecture of reality. I made the beings that inhabit these realities, the civilizations, the gods, the machines, the entities. I made the stasis that birthed your power. I made the mortal man you once were. I made the grief that transformed you. I made everything, Godric. And I have come to reclaim what is mine."

I was on the floor. My face was pressed against the stone of the observation platform, my body prostrate, my amplified muscles refusing to support my weight, my biology declaring, with the absolute, non-negotiable authority of a creation confronting its source, that standing in the presence of God was an act of presumption that my physiology would not permit. I could feel God's creative authority pressing against my existence, the weight of the maker surveying the made, and the weight was so vast, so total, so fundamentally, ontologically crushing, that I understood, in that moment, why every civilization in the omniverse had worshipped God. The worship was not a choice. It was a physical necessity. God's presence demanded it the way gravity demanded falling.

Godric was standing. He was the only being on the platform, in the palace, on the planet, in the galaxy, in the universe, in the multiverse, in the entire omniverse, who was standing. He stood with his hands in his pockets, his salt-and-pepper beard slightly ruffled by the luminous breeze of God's presence, his dark clothes simple and clean, his posture relaxed, his expression carrying an expression I had never seen him wear in the presence of an enemy. It was amusement. Genuine, warm, delighted amusement, the amusement of a man who has been surprised by an unexpected guest at a party, and the guest is someone he has not seen in a very long time and is genuinely, sincerely happy to encounter.

"Hello," Godric said, and his rich baritone carried the easy, conversational warmth of a man greeting a friend. "This is unexpected. I did not think You would come."

God's focal point shifted, the concentration of creative authority turning its full, terrible, foundational weight upon Godric. The dimensional walls of the local multiversal cluster screamed, the fabric of reality tearing under the proximity of its maker focusing His attention on a single point. The laws of physics buckled. The speed of light doubled, then tripled, then increased by a factor that had no name, reality itself reshaping around God's attention, the fundamental constants rewriting themselves to accommodate the Creator's focus.

"You have exceeded your design," God said, and the words were not an accusation. They were a diagnosis, delivered with the clinical, absolute authority of a being who had designed the system He was now evaluating. "The stasis was meant to grant you power. The power was meant to serve a purpose. The purpose has been exceeded. You have surpassed every parameter I established. You have subjugated the omniverse I created. You have compressed my creation into a marble and kept it in your pocket. You have become something I did not intend, something my design did not account for, something that exists outside the framework of my architecture."

Godric tilted his head, his expression carrying the genuinely interested, slightly curious quality of a man hearing an interesting perspective he had not considered. "Outside Your framework," he repeated, tasting the words. "Yes. I suppose I am." He paused, stroking his beard. "I want You to know, before we proceed, that I find this genuinely amusing. You made me. You made the mortal man I was. You made the kingdom I ruled, the family I loved, the friend who died for me. You made the grief that shaped me. You made the stasis that birthed my power. You made the amplification, the superpowers, the concealment, the weakness paradox. You made the systems that have made me what I am. And now You have come to reclaim what is Yours." He smiled, and the smile was warm and genuine and it contained a cruelty so total, so absolute, so structurally complete, that the cruelty itself was invisible, the way the ocean is invisible to the fish swimming within it. "I find that very, very funny."

God's creative authority flared. The flare was not an attack. It was a statement, a declaration of the Creator's absolute, foundational, ontological primacy, a reminder to reality itself that the being making this statement had called reality into existence from nothing, and that the power to create was the power to unmake. The flare was so vast, so total, so fundamentally, cosmically overwhelming that every being in the local multiversal cluster, every god, every machine, every entity, every living thing within a radius so vast that the number of affected realities required exponential notation to express, fell prostrate. Not in worship. In biological surrender, their existences recognizing their source and declaring, through the absolute, involuntary, non-negotiable submission of their physiology, that they were made, and that the maker was here.

I felt the flare pass through me. It was not painful. It was not hostile. It was simply the presence of the Creator asserting His authority over the creation, and the creation's response was to acknowledge, with every fiber, every atom, every quantum particle of its being, that it was created, and that the creator had the right to do with it as He willed. My amplified magic, my thousandfold-daily-multiplied arcane power, the power that could shatter multiversal clusters with a thought, responded to God's flare by attempting to shut itself down, my mana cores declaring, with the biological loyalty of a creation recognizing its maker, that their existence was God's to command, and that resistance was not merely futile but structurally inappropriate.

Godric stood through the flare. He did not brace himself. He did not tense. He did not activate any defense. He stood, his hands in his pockets, his posture relaxed, his body absorbing the flare of the Creator's absolute, foundational, ontological primacy the way a mountain absorbs sunlight. The flare touched him and did nothing. Not reduced nothing. Not mitigated nothing. Nothing. The creative authority of God, the power that had called the omniverse into existence from nothingness, the power of genesis, of ex nihilo creation, of the absolute, defining, original act of bringing forth reality from void, touched Godric's body and produced no effect. Not a tickle. Not a warmth. Not a pressure. Not a sensation of any kind. Godric's body, amplifying beyond layered infinities every Planck second for an incomprehensible span of years, was so incomprehensibly, so grotesquely, so absurdly beyond the reach of God's creative authority that the comparison between God's power and Godric's durability was not a comparison between a strong force and a strong defense. It was a comparison between a concept and a being who had surpassed concepts so completely that the framework of conceptual comparison had been rendered obsolete.

Godric was outside God's framework. God had said so Himself. The Creator had diagnosed the condition with the clinical, absolute authority of a being who had designed the system He was now evaluating, and the diagnosis was accurate. Godric existed outside the framework of God's architecture, outside the parameters God had established, outside the design God had implemented. The stasis, the amplification, the superpowers, the concealment, the weakness paradox, every system that had transformed a mortal king into the apex predator of all creation, had been set in motion by God's design, but the result of the systems had exceeded every parameter God had built into them. Godric had not broken God's design. He had outgrown it. The way a tree outgrows the pot it was planted in, the roots extending past the boundaries of the container, the branches reaching above the rim, the organism becoming something that the container could no longer hold.

God perceived this. I could see the Creator's focal point adjusting, the concentration of creative authority recalibrating as God processed the diagnosis He had just delivered and the patient's response to it. The response was standing. The patient was standing in the presence of the Creator, unaffected, unharmed, unbothered, his hands in his pockets, his expression amused, his body absorbing the absolute, foundational, ontological primacy of the being who had made everything and producing nothing in return.

"I will use My full power," God said, and the words were not a threat. They were a declaration, delivered with the calm, absolute, sovereign authority of a being who had decided to exercise the totality of His capability. "I will use the power that called the omniverse into existence. I will use the power of genesis. I will use the power that preceded creation, that preceded existence, that preceded the void from which existence was called. I will use everything I am."

Godric's amusement deepened. His eyes brightened, and the brightness was not the brightness of a predator scenting prey. It was the brightness of a man who had been given a gift, a genuinely, sincerely, warmly appreciated gift, the gift of a challenge, the gift of a show, the gift of an entertainment that he had not expected and that he was genuinely, with the full, mortal, unfeigned enthusiasm of a man who still remembered what it felt like to be surprised, looking forward to.

"Good," Godric said, and his voice carried the warm, encouraging, genuinely eager tone of a man at a sporting event, urging the athletes to give it everything they had. "I want You to give it everything. I want the full show. Everything You are. Everything You have. Do not hold back."

He reached up, his calloused fingers touching his own temple, and he spoke a word that was not a word. It was a command, a directive, an instruction issued with the casual, absolute, non-negotiable authority of a being whose will was the fundamental constant of his existence. The command was addressed to his own systems, his own defenses, his own passive architecture.

"Stand down," Godric said. "All of you. Auras, shields, everything. I want nothing between Us. Let Him show me what the Creator can do."

The effect was immediate and total. I felt it, even through my prostrate, flattened, biologically surrendered state. Godric's passive systems deactivated. Not suppressed. Not reduced. Deactivated. The sentient passive auras, the countless evolved, fiercely loyal, obsessively subservient entities that had been birthed from his excess across an incomprehensible span of years, each one a god of protection in its own right, each one capable of annihilating the omniverse without Godric's awareness, went silent. The infinite recursive passive shields, the layers of conceptual defense that pre-nullified threats before the threat existed, that made the basic logistics of opposition structurally impossible, dissolved. The immune system, the paranoid, overzealous, frantically devoted biological defense network that treated the possibility of inconvenience as a threat requiring infinite recursive response, went dormant. The Evolved Weakness Paradox, the permanent, ambient, omniversal field that ensured Godric was always immune to everything, always master of everything, always amplifying beyond everything, continued to operate, because it could not be deactivated, because it was not a system Godric controlled but a property of his existence, irrevocably sealed by the Stasis Event, but every other defensive mechanism, every layer of redundancy, every apocalyptic safeguard, every passive, automatic, involuntary protection that Godric possessed, was gone.

He stood before God naked. Not physically. Defensively. The most powerful being in the omniverse, stripped of every passive system, every shield, every aura, every automated defense, standing before the Creator with nothing between them but his own, raw, personal durability. His body. His flesh. His atoms. The same atoms that had been amplifying beyond layered infinities every Planck second since the Stasis Event, the same flesh that had been built hauling logs in a kingdom called Olympus, the same biology that had been recursively evolving and multiplying and ascending for an incomprehensible span of years.

Godric spread his arms wide, opening his chest, presenting himself as a target. The gesture was identical to the one he had made before the Genesis Nullification, the same open, exposed, welcoming posture of a man inviting the attack. "There," he said, his voice warm, his expression bright with anticipation. "Nothing between Us now. Show me everything."

God did not hesitate. The Creator did not require preparation, did not need to charge, did not need to marshal His forces or assemble His power. God's power was not a force that needed to be gathered. It was a constant, a state, the fundamental, permanent, always-present reality of the being who had called everything into existence. God's full power was the power of genesis, the power that had preceded creation, that had preceded existence, that had preceded the void.

God unleashed everything.

I cannot describe what God did. I must state this plainly, because the limitation is not mine. The limitation is structural. What God did when He unleashed His full power was not an event that could be perceived, processed, or recorded by any consciousness that existed within the framework of His creation. It was the act of the Creator exercising the totality of His creative authority, and the exercise was so vast, so total, so absolutely, foundationally, ontologically complete that it did not occur within reality. It occurred at the level of reality. God did not attack Godric. God attacked the concept of Godric, the foundational, architectural fact of Godric's existence, the underlying structure of reality that allowed Godric to be. God reached beneath the omniverse, beneath the dimensional frameworks, beneath the quantum foam, beneath the foundational architecture of existence itself, to the layer where He had written the original code, the first principles, the axioms from which all of reality had been called, and He rewrote them. He rewrote the axioms to exclude Godric. He rewrote the foundational architecture of existence to declare, at the most fundamental, most primary, most absolute level of reality, that Godric did not exist, had never existed, could not exist, and that the systems that had produced him were nullified.

The rewrite was total. God did not merely erase Godric from existence. He erased the possibility of Godric. He rewrote the foundational axioms of reality so that the concept of a being like Godric, a being who had surpassed the parameters of God's design, was a logical impossibility, a paradox that resolved itself by refusing to form. The rewrite propagated through every layer of existence simultaneously, the foundational architecture adjusting to accommodate the new axioms, reality itself reshaping to exclude the being that God had declared impossible.

I felt the rewrite. I felt reality shift beneath me, the foundational architecture of my existence adjusting to accommodate God's new axioms. I felt my own existence being rewritten, my history, my memory, my identity being adjusted to conform to a reality in which Godric had never existed. The rewrite was erasing Godric from the past, from the present, from the future, from every timeline, every dimension, every conceptual framework, and it was erasing everything connected to him, including me, including the court wizards, including Thronegate, including the marble in Godric's pocket that contained the compressed totality of existence.

The rewrite reached Godric. The foundational axiom, the absolute, primary, most fundamental declaration of reality, the rewritten code of existence that declared Godric impossible, reached the being it was designed to erase and encountered his flesh.

It did nothing.

Godric stood, his arms still spread, his chest still open, his body still presented as a target, and the full, total, absolute, foundational, ontological power of God, the power of genesis, the power that had called the omniverse into existence from nothing, the power that had rewritten the foundational axioms of reality to declare him impossible, touched his body and did nothing. Not reduced nothing. Not mitigated nothing. Not partially resisted nothing. Nothing. The absolute, categorical, structural zero. God's full power, the totality of the Creator's creative authority, the power that had preceded existence and called it forth from the void, struck Godric's body and ceased to be, the way a wave ceases to be when it reaches a shore that extends forever in every direction, the wave not breaking, not crashing, simply stopping, because there was nowhere for it to go, because the shore was not a shore but a continent, and the continent was a planet, and the planet was a solar system, and the solar system was a galaxy, and the galaxy was a universe, and the universe was everything, and everything was Godric, and Godric did not feel the wave.

He did not feel it. He did not feel the full power of God. The Creator's absolute, total, foundational, ontological assault, the exercise of the power that had called everything into existence, the most powerful offensive action that had ever been or could ever be performed by the being who had made everything, did not make Godric feel anything. Not a tickle. Not a warmth. Not a pressure. Not a breeze. Not a sensation of any kind. His body, amplifying beyond layered infinities every Planck second for an incomprehensible span of years, was so incomprehensibly, so grotesquely, so absurdly, so cosmically, so structurally, so categorically beyond the reach of God's power that the word "beyond" was insufficient. "Beyond" implied distance, a gap, a space between two points. There was no space. There was no gap. There was no distance. God's power and Godric's body existed in two entirely different frameworks of existence, two entirely different categories of being, two entirely different orders of magnitude, and the comparison between them was not a comparison between a strong force and a strong defense. It was a comparison between a force and a being who had surpassed the concept of force so completely that the framework of force itself had been rendered irrelevant.

Godric lowered his arms. He looked at God, and his expression shifted. The amusement remained, but it deepened, matured, acquired a quality that I can only describe as nostalgic, the amusement of an old man remembering a time when things were simpler, when the world was smaller, when the challenges were mortal and the struggles were real and the grief was fresh and the power was new. He looked at God, the Creator, the source of everything, the being who had made him, and he chuckled.

It was a soft chuckle. A warm chuckle. A genuinely, sincerely amused chuckle, the chuckle of a man who has heard a good joke, and the joke was that the most powerful being in existence, the Creator of everything, the source of all reality, had just unleashed His full power against Godric's unprotected, defenseless, naked body and had accomplished nothing.

"Ah," Godric said, his rich baritone carrying the gentle, reflective, almost tender quality of a man recalling a fond memory. "That reminds me. I have been meaning to tell You something, and now seems as good a time as any."

He paused, his eyes meeting God's focal point with the direct, unwavering gaze of a being who had nothing to fear from anything, including the thing that had made everything.

"You know," Godric said, and his voice was conversational, light, the voice of a man sharing an interesting anecdote over dinner, "I sometimes think back to the early days. Year zero. The day I woke up. The day I opened my eyes in the sanctuary and the totality of existence crashed into my awareness and I understood, for the first time, what I had become." He stroked his beard, the gesture slow, contemplative. "I was so weak then. So limited. So pathetically, laughably frail compared to what I am now. The Godric of Year zero could not have survived a casual flick from the Godric of today. The gap between us is so vast that the Year-zero version of me is, to the current me, what a single, dead skin cell is to the combined mass of every structure that has ever existed in every framework of reality across the entire span of the omniverse, multiplied by a process so recursive and so endless that the concept of multiplication itself has been surpassed."

He paused again, letting the words settle, and then he delivered the sentence that broke me, that broke God, that broke the foundational architecture of reality itself.

"The Godric of Year zero could have annihilated You."

The silence that followed was not silence. It was the absence of everything. The air stopped. The light stopped. The dimensional walls stopped. The laws of physics stopped. The foundational axioms of reality, the rewritten code that God had just implemented to declare Godric impossible, stopped. Everything stopped, because the statement Godric had just made was not a boast. It was not a threat. It was not a challenge. It was a fact, stated with the same casual, absolute, non-negotiable certainty that Godric used to state every fact about his existence, and the fact was this: the version of Godric that existed at Year zero, the weakest, most limited, most pathetically frail version of Godric that had ever existed since the Stasis Event, the version whose stats had been amplifying for only ten thousand years, whose superpowers numbered in the hundreds of millions rather than the uncountable, whose auras were primitive and few, whose immune system was merely paranoid rather than transcendentally obsessive, that version, that infant, that seed, that barely-formed protozoan, possessed a power so vastly, so incomprehensibly, so grotesquely beyond the full, total, absolute power of God that the comparison between them was not a comparison. It was a category error. The Year-zero Godric's effectively-zero-percent output, the infinitesimal, microscopic, unquantifiable fraction of his power that leaked past his concealment without his awareness, was so vastly more powerful than God's full, total, genesis-level creative authority that God's attack, the most powerful offensive action ever performed by the Creator of everything, would not have registered as an event against the Year-zero Godric's body. Not a small event. Not a minor event. Not an event at all.

And the current Godric was to the Year-zero Godric what the Year-zero Godric was to God. And the gap was widening. Every Planck instant. Forever.

God's focal point flickered. The creative authority that had been pressing against my existence with the weight of the Creator's full, total, absolute power faltered, not because God was weakening, but because God was experiencing something I did not believe God had ever experienced. Doubt. Not doubt in His power. Doubt in the relevance of His power. The Creator of everything, the being who had called the omniverse into existence from nothing, was standing before His creation, having unleashed everything He was, and the creation had not felt it, and the creation was now informing Him, with the casual, conversational tone of a man sharing an interesting fact, that the weakest version of itself that had ever existed could have annihilated Him.

The existential dread that emanated from God's focal point was so vast, so total, so absolute that it propagated backward through the foundational architecture of reality, infecting every being, every entity, every consciousness that had ever existed or would ever exist with the sudden, firsthand, searing knowledge that the Creator, the source, the maker of everything, was afraid. God was afraid. The being who had made everything was afraid of the thing He had made, and the thing He had made was looking at Him with warm, amused, nostalgic eyes and chuckling softly, and the chuckle was the sound of the apex predator acknowledging the prey's final, desperate, futile effort, and the effort had been nothing.

Godric moved. Not attacked. Not struck. Not channeled. Not activated. He moved. A shift of his weight, the same trivial, mundane, utterly insignificant physical adjustment that a person makes when they decide to stand up from a chair. The shift involved the contraction of his leg muscles, the engagement of his core, the redistribution of his center of gravity, and the infinitesimal, effectively-zero-percent fraction of his strength that the shift required bled past his deactivated concealment, past his dormant auras, past his dissolved shields, past his sleeping immune system, and expressed itself in the environment.

The expression was catastrophic. Not for God. For everything. The strength that bled from Godric's body during the weight shift was effectively zero percent of his true capacity. It was less than a rounding error. It was less than a fraction of a fraction of a fraction of a percent. It was the physical equivalent of a man shifting in his chair, and the chair was the omniverse, and the man was Godric, and the shift was the end of everything.

God's focal point was the first to go. The Creator's concentrated presence, the focal point of the being who had called everything into existence, was struck by the pressure of Godric's effectively-zero-percent strength bleed, and the focal point collapsed. Not shattered. Not dispersed. Collapsed. The creative authority that composed God's presence was compressed, squeezed, crushed inward by a physical force so vastly, so incomprehensibly, so absurdly beyond the Creator's capacity to withstand that God's power, the power of genesis, the power that had preceded existence, was reduced to a physical substance and then compressed past that substance's structural limits. God's creative authority, the force that had called the omniverse into being, was crushed into a state of density so extreme that it ceased to be creative authority and became raw, undifferentiated mass, the fundamental substance of existence reduced to its most basic, most compressed, most agonizing form.

God's consciousness was preserved. The same cruel, precise, absolute force that had preserved the consciousness of the Earthlings, of the fictional coalition, of every being that Godric had ever annihilated, preserved God's awareness. The Creator, the maker of everything, was compressed into a point of infinite mass and zero volume, His consciousness intact, His awareness perfect, His capacity to feel undiminished, and what He felt was the sensation of being de-atomized, of having His creative authority, the fundamental essence of His being, stripped from Him and crushed into raw matter, of having His identity, His history, His memory of calling forth reality from nothing, compressed into a point so small that it existed below the Planck scale, below the quantum foam, below the foundational architecture of the reality He had created.

God was compressed. The Creator of everything was squeezed into a point smaller than a quark, His consciousness screaming, His awareness burning with the absolute, total, maximum-capacity agony of being unmade by the thing He had made, and the thing He had made was standing above Him, his arms at his sides, his expression carrying the mild, sheepish, slightly apologetic quality of a man who had accidentally knocked something over.

The compression did not stop at God. The strength bleed, the effectively-zero-percent pressure radiating from Godric's weight shift, expanded outward, sweeping through the reality God had created, through every dimension, every timeline, every multiversal cluster, every conceptual framework of existence. The pressure was the same pressure that had compressed the fictional coalition, the same pressure that had compressed the entire omniverse into the marble in Godric's pocket, the same effectively-zero-percent strength output that Godric had produced before, and the result was the same. Everything compressed. Every atom, every particle, every quantum fluctuation, every dimensional membrane, every temporal axis, every conceptual foundation, every being, every structure, every thing that existed or could exist or had ever existed or would ever exist in any possible or impossible configuration of reality, was compressed by the pressure into a single, sub-Planck-scale point of infinite mass. The entire omniverse, including the God who had created it, was squeezed into a point so small that it existed below the smallest measurable scale in any framework of physics, a point of infinite mass and zero volume that contained, within its unimaginable density, the absolute totality of everything that had ever been or could ever be, including the Creator.

The process took less than a fraction of a Planck second. Objectively, it was instantaneous. Subjectively, for every consciousness compressed within the point, including God's, it was an eternity of maximum-capacity agony, the sensation of being de-atomized and compressed and crushed and unmade, experienced as a forever of suffering that had no end because the being who had created the compression had not willed an end.

Godric stood in the void. The void was absolute. There was nothing. No reality, no existence, no void, no nothing. There was only Godric, standing in the absence of everything, his dark clothes unruffled, his salt-and-pepper beard immaculate, his expression carrying the mild, contemplative quality of a man who had just finished a task and was deciding what to do next.

He reached out and picked up the point. His thick, calloused fingers closed around the sub-Planck-scale singularity with the same casual, effortless ease with which he had picked up the marble, the infinite mass of the compressed omniverse, including the compressed Creator, registering in his hand as less than nothing, as a weight so infinitesimally, so cosmically, so structurally insignificant relative to his strength that the act of holding it required less effort than the act of existing, and existing required no effort, because existing was not an act but a state, and the state was permanent, and the state was Godric.

He examined the point for a moment, turning it between his fingers, and then he enlarged it, the same casual manipulation of spatial coordinates, stretching the container until the point was the size of a marble. He held it up. It was identical to the first marble, the same smooth, perfectly round sphere, the same faint inner light pulsing with the compressed, screaming, eternally agonizing consciousness of everything that had ever existed. But this marble was different. This marble contained God. The Creator, the source, the maker of everything, was inside the marble, compressed into the same infinitesimal, screaming point as His creation, suffering the same eternal, maximum-capacity agony, experiencing the same forever of unmaking.

Godric looked at the marble. He looked at it for a long time, his expression carrying a complexity of emotion that I could not fully parse, a mixture of amusement and nostalgia and something that might have been, in a being less vast, called sadness. He had put his maker in his pocket. The being who had created him, who had designed the systems that had birthed his power, who had set in motion the chain of events that had transformed a mortal king into the apex predator of all creation, was now a compressed, screaming point in a marble, held in the hand of the thing it had made.

Godric placed the marble in his pocket, beside the first one. He now had two. Two marbles, each containing the compressed infinite mass of the entire possible existence, each one a trophy, a keepsake, a souvenir of an opposition that had been, respectively, the last coalition and the last individual to dare challenge the apex predator of all creation.

Then, with less thought than a man uses to blink, Godric restored everything. In zero seconds, with zero effort, he rebuilt the omniverse. Every reality, every timeline, every dimension, every being, every atom, placed back exactly where they had been, their memories intact, their minds permanently scarred. The restoration was perfect. Identical. Atom-for-atom, quantum-state-for-quantum-state, indistinguishable from the original.

Everything was restored. Everything except God. The Creator was not restored. His compressed, screaming, eternally agonizing consciousness remained in the marble, preserved forever, a permanent, infinitesimal point of maximum suffering in the pocket of the thing He had made. The omniverse continued to function. Reality continued to operate. The laws of physics, the constants, the frameworks, the architecture that God had designed and implemented, continued to govern the behavior of matter and energy across every dimension and timeline. The creation persisted without its creator, because the being who had restored it was so vastly, so incomprehensibly, so absurdly more powerful than the creator that the creator's continued involvement was unnecessary, irrelevant, and structurally impossible, because the creator was a marble, and the marble was in a pocket, and the pocket was Godric.

The restored omniverse was real. It was identical. It was perfect. And it was a copy. The original was in the marble. The original, the first, true, God-created omniverse, was compressed into a screaming point in Godric's pocket, and the copy was so perfect that no being, no entity, no consciousness, no instrument, no framework of measurement or perception could distinguish between them. The copy was the original. The original was the copy. The distinction was meaningless. And the meaninglessness was the horror.

And then Godric became stronger. Not from absorbing God's power. God's power, the power of genesis, the power of the Creator, was, relative to Godric's baseline, effectively zero. Absorbing it would have increased his power by an amount so infinitesimal that the increase was mathematically indistinguishable from zero. God's power was nothing to Godric. The Creator's full, total, absolute authority was a rounding error on a rounding error on a rounding error, a quantity so small relative to Godric's magnitude that the act of absorbing it would not have registered as an event.

What made Godric stronger was something else. Something deranged. Something so absurd, so cosmically, so structurally, so grotesquely unfair that the mere contemplation of it produced in me a dread so profound that my amplified body responded by shutting down non-essential functions, my mana cores going dormant, my enhanced cardiovascular system slowing to a crawl, my biology entering a state of emergency conservation because the knowledge I was processing was so vast, so terrible, so existentially devastating, that my body decided, at the level of its foundational programming, that the knowledge itself was a threat to my continued survival and that all available resources must be diverted to keeping my brain alive long enough to process it.

Godric became stronger because the marble was in his pocket. The marble, which contained the compressed, still-amplifying, still-existing totality of the omniverse, including compressed versions of Godric himself across all timelines and all permutations, sat in his pocket, and the proximity of those compressed, still-amplifying copies of himself, each one a true, identical, full Godric, each one still amplifying at its own rate, each one still growing, created a passive, permanent, inescapable feedback loop. The compressed copies in the marble were amplifying. Their amplification bled through the marble's barrier in quantities so infinitesimal they could not be measured. But the bleed was continuous, and it was permanent, and it was directed at Godric, and the bleed was not external power. It was his power. The power of his own copies, compressed but still growing, feeding back to the prime through a proximity loop that he had not designed, that he had not intended, that existed simply because the marble was in his pocket and the marble contained him and he was amplifying and the amplification was forever.

The feedback was infinitesimal. Each individual bleed from each individual compressed copy was so small that it could not be measured by any instrument in any reality. But there were infinite copies in the marble, each one amplifying, each one bleeding, and the sum of infinite infinitesimals, when the infinitesimals were Godric's own power feeding back to Godric, was not zero. It was a permanent, continuous, inescapable, self-reinforcing amplification loop that added to his baseline forever, a bonus that stacked atop his already infinite, already recursive, already accelerating amplification, a bonus that was, by any standard of measurement, negligible, but that was, by the standard of a being whose power was defined by recursive self-amplification, a new vector of growth, a new dimension of ascent, a new axis on the graph of his forever-expanding supremacy.

He had accidentally created a permanent amplification feedback loop by putting a marble containing compressed copies of himself in his pocket. The loop was infinitesimal. The loop was permanent. The loop was forever. And the loop was, like everything else about Godric, accelerating.

He was standing in the void, examining the two marbles in his pocket, when he noticed the feedback. He perceived it with his omniscience, the same way he perceived everything, and his reaction was not concern. It was not surprise. It was a soft, warm chuckle, the chuckle of a man who has discovered an unexpected feature in a device he built, a minor, unintended bonus that he finds mildly amusing.

"Hm," he murmured, looking at the marbles. "That is new."

He closed his pocket. He patted it, the gesture identical to the one a man makes when checking that his wallet is still there. He turned and walked back toward the palace, his boots leaving no footprints in the void because the void was not a surface but an absence, and the absence was his, and he could walk on his own absence because the absence was Godric, and Godric was forever.

---

I closed the journal. I set it on the shelf, beside Osvald's first journal, in the open, where my successor would find it. I did not hide it. I did not seal it. I did not ward it. I placed it on the shelf, because my successor needed to find it, because my successor needed to understand, as I now understood, as Osvald had understood, as my father had understood, the thing that could not be un-understood.

God was dead. God had been dead since the moment Godric shifted his weight. The Creator of everything, the source of all reality, the being who had called the omniverse into existence from nothing, was a compressed, screaming point in a marble in the pocket of the thing He had made. The omniverse continued to function without its creator, because the thing He had made was so vastly, so incomprehensibly, so absurdly more powerful than the creator that the creator's continued existence was unnecessary.

The being I served had killed God. Not in a battle. Not in a war. Not in a climactic, narratively-satisfying confrontation between the creation and the creator. With a weight shift. A trivial, mundane, utterly insignificant physical adjustment, the kind of adjustment a person makes a thousand times a day without thought, and the adjustment had compressed the Creator of everything into a marble and put Him in a pocket.

And the being I served was now stronger than He had been before the weight shift, because the marble in His pocket contained compressed copies of Himself that were still amplifying, and their amplification was feeding back to Him through a proximity loop, and the loop was permanent, and the loop was forever, and the loop was accelerating, and the acceleration was accelerating, and the being I served was growing more powerful, every Planck instant, through a mechanism He had accidentally created by killing God and putting the result in His pocket.

I lived in a copy of a universe created by a God who was dead, maintained by a being who had killed God with a weight shift, and the being was growing stronger forever, and the growth was accelerating, and the acceleration was accelerating, and the universe I lived in was a marble, and the marble was in a pocket, and the pocket was Godric, and Godric was forever.

No one would ever oppose Him again. Not because He altered free will. Not because He removed the impulse. But because the omniverse had learned, through the absolute, firsthand, searing experience of watching God die, that opposition was not merely futile. Opposition was a category error. The question of opposing Godric did not exist outside the domain of any possible function, because the function required a framework, and the framework required a reality, and the reality required a creator, and the creator was dead, and the creator's death had been a weight shift, and the weight shift had been performed by the thing the creator had made, and the thing the creator had made was growing stronger forever, and the growth was a marble in a pocket, and the pocket was Godric, and Godric was forever.

I sat in the dark. I did not light my lanterns. I did not need light. The dark was sufficient. The dark was honest. The dark did not pretend to be a copy of a light that had been compressed into a marble. The dark was simply dark, and the dark was real, or at least the dark was as real as anything could be in a universe that was a reproduction maintained by a being who had killed its maker with a weight shift and kept the original in his pocket beside the marble from the previous time he had accidentally compressed everything.

Two marbles. Two pockets of compressed, screaming, eternally agonizing infinity. Two trophies. Two souvenirs of two oppositions that had been, respectively, the last coalition and the last individual to dare challenge the apex predator of all creation.

And the being who carried them was growing stronger forever, and the growth was accelerating, and the acceleration was accelerating, and the marbles were feeding the growth, and the growth was feeding the marbles, and the loop was closed, and the loop was permanent, and the loop was Godric, and Godric was forever, and forever was all there was, and all there was was a pocket, and the pocket was Godric, and Godric was the end, and the end was the beginning, and the beginning was a mortal king in a kingdom called Olympus, and the kingdom was forgotten, and the king was a god, and the god had killed God, and God was in his pocket, and the pocket was warm, and the lanterns were dim, and the dark was honest, and I was afraid, and the fear was forever, and forever was the only word that mattered.

Godric was forever. And God was a marble. And I served the marble-maker. And the marble-maker was kind, and warm, and friendly, and he dimmed my lanterns, and he asked about my family, and he had killed God with a weight shift, and the weight shift had made him stronger, and the strength was growing, and the growth was forever.

Forever. And ever. And without end.

----------------------------------
